Written by a participant of the expedition, Pigafetta\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nrelation has a greater value than any other narrative of the voyage.\r\nIts great value and the fact that it has never been adequately\r\npresented to the English-speaking public have induced the editors to\r\ninsert this relation in the present series both in the original Italian\r\n(rigidly adhering to and preserving all the peculiarities of the\r\noriginal manuscript) and in English translation. This relation is\r\nespecially valuable for its descriptions of the various peoples,\r\ncountries, and products, of Oriental seas, and for its vocabularies, as\r\nwell as for its account of the first circumnavigation. From its very\r\nnature, the relation has called for an unusual amount of annotation,\r\nwhich has been drawn freely from various sources: chiefly Mosto\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nannotations in his publication of Pigafetta\xe2\x80\x99s relation in Part V,\r\nvolume iii, of the Raccolta di documenti e studi, published by the\r\nRoyal Columbian Commission of the fourth centenary of the discovery of\r\nAmerica under the auspices of the Minister of Public Instruction (Roma,\r\n1894); Navarrete\xe2\x80\x99s Col. de viages, iv (Madrid, 1837); various\r\npublications of the Hakluyt Society; and F. H. H. Guillemard\xe2\x80\x99s Life\r\nof Ferdinand Magellan (New York, 1891). The publication of the original\r\nItalian and the English, page for page, renders it necessary to place\r\nthe annotations at the end of the volume instead of in footnote as\r\nhitherto. The various charts of the Italian manuscript are all\r\npresented in facsimile in the course of the work. In order that the\r\nvarious peculiarities of the manuscript might be preserved, it has been\r\nnecessary to specially design and cast certain characters that appear\r\nin Pigafetta\xe2\x80\x99s narrative. None of these characters have been\r\nreproduced by Mosto, who also writes out all abbreviations. Throughout\r\nwe have aimed to present the document as it exists in the Biblioteca\r\nAmbrosiana (even to the spacing of words) with the exception that\r\nparagraphs in the manuscript begin with a hanging indention and usually\r\nend with a series of dots and dashes. A brief synopsis of the relation\r\nfollows.\r\n\r\nAfter a brief dedication to the grand master of the Hospitaler knights\r\nof Rhodes or Malta, as they were called later, and of which order he is\r\na member, Pigafetta relates that, being at Barcelona in 1519 with the\r\npapal legate, he first hears of the expedition about to set out under\r\nMagalh\xc3\xa3es. Being desirous of seeing the world, he gains permission to\r\naccompany the expedition, and soon joins the fleet at Seville, whence\r\nit is to depart. Magalh\xc3\xa3es, as a wise commander, issues his\r\ninstructions to the various commanders of the vessels ere port is left,\r\nso that they may keep together in the unknown seas before them, and\r\nthat they may act in harmony.\r\n\r\nSetting sail from Seville on August 10, 1519, the fleet of five small\r\nvessels starts on its long journey amid salvos of artillery. At the\r\nmouth of the Guadalquivir, San Lucar de Barrameda, they anchor until\r\nSeptember 20, when setting sail once more, they make for the Canaries,\r\nwhich are reached September 26. There they reprovision and taking their\r\ndeparture on October 3, coast southward along Africa amid alternating\r\ncalms and violent storms (cheered however by the welcome apparition of\r\nSt. Elmo\xe2\x80\x99s fire, which promises them safety), until they cross the\r\nline. Thereupon taking a general westerly course, the cape of St.\r\nAugustine on the Brazilian coast is soon sighted. The fresh provisions,\r\nso essential to sea voyages, are procured on the coast of Brazil, where\r\noccurs the first communication with the natives, with whom wonderful\r\nbargains are made. Those Indians, cannibals though they be, and whom\r\nPigafetta describes briefly (not failing to inscribe some of their\r\nlanguage) receive the mariners hospitably, and thinking that the latter\r\nare come to remain among them, build them a house. But after a stay of\r\neighteen days, the sails are again trimmed toward the south, and\r\ndescending the coast, Magalh\xc3\xa3es anchors next at the Rio de la Plata\r\nwhich had formerly proved so disastrous to Juan de Solis and his men.\r\nUnable here to hold converse with the anthropophagous natives, who flee\r\nat their approach, the fleet retakes its course, anchoring at two\r\nislands where many sea-wolves and penguins are taken, and thus fresh\r\nfood obtained. The next anchorage is at the famous Bay of St. Julian\r\nalong the desolate Patagonian coast, where for five months they winter.\r\nFor two months not an individual is seen, but one day they gain their\r\nfirst sight of the Patagonians, whose huge bulk strikes all with\r\nsurprise, and who are held as giants. Amicable relations are entered\r\ninto with various of these wandering Indians, and finally Magalh\xc3\xa3es,\r\nwith the taste for the wonderful that characterized his period, as\r\nstrongly, or more strongly than our own, determines to capture two of\r\nthem to take back to Spain as novelties. His ruse is successful, but an\r\nattempt to induce the wife of one of the Indians to go to the ship\r\nfails. Very interesting are these giants to the curious Pigafetta, and\r\nto him is due the earliest description of their manners and customs and\r\nthe earliest specimens of their language. The two captured giants are\r\nplaced in separate vessels, but unfortunately both die ere reaching the\r\nend of the journey, one in the deserting ship \xe2\x80\x9cSan Antonio,\xe2\x80\x9d and\r\nthe other in Magalh\xc3\xa3es\xe2\x80\x99s own ship, the \xe2\x80\x9cTrinidad.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nDuring the five months at that port \xe2\x80\x9cmany things happened there.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\nShortly after entering the port, the most critical moment of all\r\nMagalh\xc3\xa3es\xe2\x80\x99s life comes, and one which he has perhaps, dreaded from\r\nthe beginning of the expedition. This is the mutiny headed by Juan de\r\nCartagena, captain of one of the vessels, and other malcontents, who\r\nhate Magalh\xc3\xa3es because he is a Portuguese. The latter, however, proves\r\nequal to the emergency, and by his prompt action and the punishments\r\ntempered by mercy that he inflicts, quiets the trouble. Jo\xc3\xa3o Serr\xc3\xa3o,\r\ncaptain of the \xe2\x80\x9cSantiago\xe2\x80\x9d is sent to explore the coast, but is\r\nshipwrecked, although all the crew are saved. Their rescue (not well\r\ntold by Pigafetta) is a thrilling and arduous matter, and calls into\r\nplay the endurance of men already tried by misfortune and buffetings\r\nwith Nature.\r\n\r\nWith the fleet reduced to four vessels, the mariners leave port St.\r\nJulian and proceeding along the coast, anchor at the river of Sardines,\r\nwhere stormy weather threatens a disastrous end to the expedition. A\r\nstay of two months is made, during which the ships are enabled to lay\r\nin a good supply of provisions, wood, and water. Before leaving that\r\nriver, the crews (for Magalh\xc3\xa3es looks after the spiritual welfare of\r\nhis men) confess and take communion. Then resuming the voyage, the\r\ngreat object of the first half of the expedition is attained, namely,\r\nthe discovery of the strait, which occurs October 21, 1520. \xe2\x80\x9cThat\r\nstrait is one hundred and ten leguas ... long, and it is one-half legua\r\nbroad, more or less.\xe2\x80\x9d Its discovery is due to the indomitable energy\r\nand endurance of Magalh\xc3\xa3es, and his certain knowledge (probably\r\noverstated by Pigafetta) of its existence. Continuing, Pigafetta\r\nbriefly narrates the passage through the strait, and the desertion of\r\nthe \xe2\x80\x9cSan Antonio,\xe2\x80\x9d which returns to Spain, after putting the\r\ncaptain, Alvaro de Mesquita, a relative of Magalh\xc3\xa3es, in irons; for\r\nthe pilot, a Portuguese named Esteban Gomez, is jealous of Magalh\xc3\xa3es,\r\nas the latter\xe2\x80\x99s expedition has destroyed ambitious plans of his own.\r\nThe other three ships, leaving letters and signals in the strait, in\r\ncase the \xe2\x80\x9cSan Antonio\xe2\x80\x9d tries to regain them, proceeds on its way,\r\ndebouching from the strait November 28. Then begins a long voyage over\r\nthe trackless Pacific \xe2\x80\x9cin truth ... very pacific;\xe2\x80\x9d and the three\r\nships sail on steadily for three and two-thirds months without being\r\nable to reprovision. To the horrors of famine are added the sufferings\r\nof the dread scurvy. Pigafetta, whose curiosity is always alert and\r\nactive, and who remains well, diverts himself with talking to the\r\nPatagonian, who is finally baptized, but who is one of those to die. In\r\nthe vast stretch from the strait to the Ladrones (first seen by them of\r\nall Europeans), only two islands, both desert, are sighted, and those,\r\nsince they are unable to find anchorage there, are called the\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cUnfortunate Isles.\xe2\x80\x9d Pigafetta mentions the southern constellation\r\nCrux and the star clouds since called after Magalh\xc3\xa3es. His\r\ngeographical information, as one might expect, is not always accurate,\r\nfor he places Cipangu (Japan) in the open Pacific. Thoughts of relief\r\nthat come upon sighting various islands (which they called the Ladrones\r\nbecause of the thievishness of the inhabitants) are quickly dissipated\r\nby the hostility there encountered. So bold are these natives (whose\r\nappearance, life, and customs, Pigafetta describes briefly), that they\r\neven steal the ship\xe2\x80\x99s boat from the stern of the \xe2\x80\x9cTrinidad,\xe2\x80\x9d thus\r\nnecessitating a raid into one of the islands, where some of the natives\r\nare killed, and some houses burned, but the boat recovered.\r\n\r\nOn March 16, 1521, the first of the Philippines (by them called the\r\narchipelago of San Lazaro) to be seen by Europeans, is sighted. Anchor\r\nis cast at a small desert island called Humunu, (but which the mariners\r\ncall \xe2\x80\x9cThe watering-place of good signs\xe2\x80\x9d because the first traces of\r\ngold are found there), near Samar, where two tents are quickly set up\r\nfor the sick, whom Magalh\xc3\xa3es himself tends with solicitude. March 18,\r\nthey gain their first acquaintance with the natives, who prove\r\nhospitable, and promise fresh provisions. These are brought on the\r\ntwenty-second of March, and the Europeans have their first sight of a\r\ntattooed Visayan chief, who, as well as his men, is decked out in gold\r\nornaments. After a week\xe2\x80\x99s stay, the ships again set sail, Pigafetta\r\nalmost coming to an untimely end by slipping over the side of the\r\nvessel while fishing, but happily saved by the aid of \xe2\x80\x9cthat fount of\r\nmercy,\xe2\x80\x9d the Virgin.\r\n\r\nMarch 28, anchor is cast at the island of Limasaua (Mazava), where\r\nEnrique, the Malaccan slave of Magalh\xc3\xa3es, serves as interpreter.\r\nAmicable relations are speedily entered into and confirmed by the\r\nMalayan rite of blood brotherhood. The king of Limasaua, and his\r\nbrother, the king of certain districts in Mindanao, prove most helpful,\r\nand are completely won over by a judicious presentation of gifts.\r\nGreatly are the natives impressed by the power of the new comers, as\r\nseen in the artillery and armor, and their astonishment is increased\r\nwhen Magalh\xc3\xa3es relates his course to their islands and the discovery\r\nof the strait.\r\n\r\nOn Good Friday, Pigafetta and a companion visit the natives ashore,\r\nwhere they spend the night in the king\xe2\x80\x99s palace, a typical Visayan\r\nhouse raised aloft on supports and thatched with nipa. Here the various\r\nceremonies that he witnesses impress Pigafetta, and his companion, cast\r\nin coarser mould than he, becomes intoxicated. Pigafetta, always\r\ninterested in the language of the new peoples whom he meets, writes\r\ndown certain of their words, whereat they are greatly astonished. He\r\nrecords that he \xe2\x80\x9cate meat on Holy Friday, for I could not help\r\nmyself.\xe2\x80\x9d On Easter Sunday, the natives are deeply impressed by the\r\nmass that is celebrated ashore, and the cross which is planted in the\r\nhighest part of the island, and which they promise to adore.\r\n\r\nThe limited amount of food in Limasaua, which is used only as a place\r\nof recreation by the two kings, who go there to visit one another and\r\nhunt, leads Magalh\xc3\xa3es to seek a more abundant harbor. Among the places\r\npointed out where food is abundant is the island of Ceb\xc3\xba, and there\r\nMagalh\xc3\xa3es determines to go, \xe2\x80\x9cfor so did his unhappy fate will.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\nAfter a seven days\xe2\x80\x99 stay at Limasaua, the course is laid to Ceb\xc3\xba\r\nunder the pilotage of the king of Limasaua, who is finally taken aboard\r\nthe \xe2\x80\x9cTrinidad\xe2\x80\x9d as his vessel is unable to keep up with the\r\nswifter-moving European vessels. Entering the port of Ceb\xc3\xba on April 7,\r\namid the thunder of their guns, the settlement is thrown into\r\nconsternation, but the Malaccan being sent ashore reassures them of his\r\nmaster\xe2\x80\x99s good intentions, whom he proclaims to be a \xe2\x80\x9ccaptain of the\r\ngreatest king and prince in the world,\xe2\x80\x9d who \xe2\x80\x9cwas going to discover\r\nMalucho,\xe2\x80\x9d but hearing of the great fame of the king of Ceb\xc3\xba, wishes\r\ntrade with him. The king of Ceb\xc3\xba is willing to accord friendship to\r\nthe Europeans, but asks a tribute, as it is the custom for all visitors\r\nto pay it to him. But no tribute will be paid him, asserts Enrique, and\r\nthe king, at the advice of a Moro merchant who has heard of the deeds\r\nof the Portuguese along Malacca and the Indian coast, and confuses the\r\nstrangers with them, until undeceived by Enrique (who declares them to\r\nbe much greater than the Portuguese), expresses his willingness to make\r\nfriendship with Magalh\xc3\xa3es. With the help of the friendly king of\r\nLimasaua, peace is made according to Malay rites, and gifts exchanged.\r\nMagalh\xc3\xa3es, deeply religious, in common with many of his age, early\r\nseeks to lure the natives of Ceb\xc3\xba to holy baptism, by presenting to\r\nthem its most attractive side, and promising the king if he becomes a\r\nChristian, a suit of armor; but they must become willing converts, and\r\nnot for the hope of gain or for fear. The peace is more firmly cemented\r\nby the visit of Pigafetta and a companion to the king, where they\r\nwitness ceremonies similar to those of Limasaua, and where gifts are\r\nbestowed upon the king and some others. They also visit the house of\r\nthe prince apparent, where they hear their first concert of Visayan\r\nmusic and see a native dance. On the following Wednesday two of the\r\ncrew are buried ashore on consecrated ground with as much pomp as\r\npossible.\r\n\r\nTrading is instituted by carrying a quantity of merchandise ashore, the\r\nsafety of which is assured by the king. Those people are found to have\r\nweights and measures for their trading; and besides their gongs, a\r\nflute-like instrument. Their houses are entered by ladders. On Friday\r\nbegins the trading, gold being given for metals and large articles, and\r\nfood for the smaller wares. The good bargains obtained by the\r\nEuropeans, would have been materially less and the trade spoiled\r\nforever had it not been for Magalh\xc3\xa3es\xe2\x80\x99s watchfulness, for so eager\r\nare the men at the sight of the gold, that they would have given almost\r\nanything for it. On the following Sunday, the king and his chief men,\r\nand the queen and many women, are baptized and given European names,\r\nand ere the week closes all the Cebuans have become Christians, as well\r\nas some from neighboring islands. The queen at her earnest request, is\r\ngiven a small image of the Christ child, the same afterward recovered\r\nby Legazpi, and still held in the greatest of reverence at Ceb\xc3\xba. The\r\nopposition of certain chiefs to the king of Ceb\xc3\xba is satisfactorily\r\nended by the inducements and threats of Magalh\xc3\xa3es. The latter swears\r\nto be faithful in his friendship with the natives, who likewise swear\r\nallegiance to the king of Spain. However, the natives are loath to\r\ndestroy their idols, according to their promise, and Magalh\xc3\xa3es finds\r\nthem still sacrificing to them for the cure of sickness. Substituting\r\ntherefore the assurance that the new faith will work a cure, in lieu of\r\nwhich he offers his head, the sick man (who is the prince\xe2\x80\x99s brother\r\nand the bravest and wisest man in the island) is miraculously cured.\r\nThereupon many idols are burned amid great demonstrations. Vivid\r\ndescriptions are given of the people and their customs and ceremonies,\r\nespecially those of sacrifice and mourning.\r\n\r\nApril 20, a chief from the neighboring island of Mactan sends a small\r\npresent to Magalh\xc3\xa3es, with the request to aid him with a boat load of\r\nmen against the chief Cilapulapu, who refuses allegiance to Spain.\r\nMagalh\xc3\xa3es in his ardor, and notwithstanding the remonstrances of his\r\nfriends, leads three boat loads of men (sixty in all) to the island,\r\nwhere having ordered the king of Ceb\xc3\xba to be a witness of the battle\r\nonly, he engages the natives. Disastrous indeed does that day prove,\r\nfor beset by multitudes of foes, the Europeans are compelled to\r\nretreat, and the retreat becomes a rout, the personal bravery of\r\nMagalh\xc3\xa3es and a few of his closest friends only saving the men from\r\nalmost complete massacre. Recognizing the leader, the natives make\r\ntheir greatest efforts against him, and finally he is killed while knee\r\ndeep in the water, but after all the others are saved. Pigafetta\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nlament is tragic and sorrowful; they \xe2\x80\x9ckilled our mirror, our light,\r\nour comfort, and our true guide.\xe2\x80\x9d Insolent in their victory, the\r\nnatives refuse to give up the body of the slain leader at the request\r\nof the king of Ceb\xc3\xba. The Europeans stunned by the loss of their\r\nleader, withdraw their merchandise and guards to the ship, and make\r\npreparations for departure. Duarte Barbosa and Jo\xc3\xa3o de Serr\xc3\xa3o are\r\nchosen leaders. The second act in the drama follows speedily. The slave\r\nEnrique, enraged at a severe reprimand and threats by Barbosa,\r\nconspires with the king of Ceb\xc3\xba; with the result that twenty-six men,\r\nincluding both of the leaders, are murdered at a banquet on May 1, to\r\nwhich the king invites them. Jo\xc3\xa3o Carvalho, deaf to the entreaties of\r\nJo\xc3\xa3o Serr\xc3\xa3o, his comrade, and anxious to become leader, sails away\r\nleaving him to his death. Pigafetta names the products of Ceb\xc3\xba, and\r\ngives a valuable vocabulary of Visayan words, most of which are still\r\nin use by those people.\r\n\r\nBy mutual consent, the three vessels proceed to Bohol, where the\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cConcepcion\xe2\x80\x9d is burned, as there are too few men left to work all\r\nthree ships; although its supplies and all else possible are\r\ntransferred to the \xe2\x80\x9cVictoria\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cTrinidad.\xe2\x80\x9d Then, cruising\r\nalong, they put in at Mindanao where Pigafetta goes ashore alone, after\r\nthe king has made blood friendship at the ships. There they hear of\r\nLuz\xc3\xb3n, where the Chinese trade annually. Departing from Mindanao, they\r\nanchor at Cagayan Sulu, a penal settlement for Borneo, where the\r\nblowpipe and poisoned arrows are used, and the daggers adorned with\r\ngold. The next anchorage is at Paragua, although before reaching that\r\nisland, the men have been tempted to abandon the ships because of\r\nhunger. There the rice is cooked under the fire in bamboos and is\r\nbetter than that cooked in earthen pots. Those people raise fighting\r\ncocks and bet on their favorite birds. Ten leagues from Paragua is the\r\ngreat island of Borneo, whither the ships next go, and anchor at the\r\ncity of Brunei, which is built over the water, and contains twenty-five\r\nthousand fires. Hospitably received by eight chiefs who visit the\r\nships, they enter into relations with the Borneans. Seven men go as\r\nambassadors to visit the king, and bear presents to him and the chief\r\nmen. Here some of the grandeurs of an oriental court are spread before\r\ntheir eyes, which Pigafetta briefly describes. The strangers are\r\ngraciously given permission to take on fresh supplies of food, water,\r\nand wood, and to trade at pleasure. Later actions of the Borneans cause\r\nthe men of the ships to fear treachery, and forestalling any action by\r\nthat people, they attack a number of junks near them, and capture four.\r\nAmong the captives is the son of the king of Luz\xc3\xb3n, who is the chief\r\ncaptain in Borneo, and whom Carvalho allows to escape, without\r\nconsulting the others, for a large sum of gold. His action in so doing\r\nreacts on himself, for the king refuses to allow two men who were\r\nashore and Carvalho\xe2\x80\x99s own son (born of a native woman in Brazil) to\r\nreturn to the ships, and they are left behind. The Borneans and their\r\njunks are described. They use porcelain dishes which are made from a\r\nfine white clay that is buried under ground for fifty years in order to\r\nrefine it, and inherited from father to son. Camphor is obtained there,\r\nand the island is so large that it can be circumnavigated by a prau\r\nonly in three months\xe2\x80\x99 time.\r\n\r\nOn leaving Borneo, a number of prisoners from the captured junks are\r\nkept, among them three women whom Carvalho ostensibly retains as\r\npresents for the queen of Spain, but in reality for himself. Happily\r\nescaping from the point on which one of the ships has become grounded,\r\nand the fear of explosion from a candle which is snuffed into a barrel\r\nof powder, the ships anchor at a point of Borneo, where for forty-two\r\ndays, the men are busied in repairing, calking, and furnishing the\r\nvessels. The journey is resumed back toward Paragua, the governor of a\r\ndistrict of that island being captured on the way; with whom, however,\r\nthey enter into friendly relations. Thence the ships cruise along\r\nbetween Cagayan, Jol\xc3\xb3, and Mindanao, capturing a native boat from\r\nMaingdanao of the latter island, from the captive occupants of which\r\nthey learn news of the Moluccas. Pushing on amid stormy weather, they\r\nanchor at the island of Sarangani, just south of Mindanao; and thence\r\nproceed in a generally southerly direction amid many islands until the\r\nMoluccas are reached, and they enter the harbor of Tidore on Friday,\r\nNovember 8, 1521, after twenty-seven months, less two days, since their\r\ndeparture from Spain.\r\n\r\nAt Tidore a warm welcome awaits them from the king, who is a powerful\r\nastrologer and has been expecting their arrival. He promises them as\r\nmany cloves as they wish, even offering to go outside his island,\r\ncontrary to the practice of kings, to provide them the sooner; in\r\nreturn for his services hoping for their aid in his designs for power\r\nin the Moluccas, especially against the king of Ternate. There they\r\nlearn that Francisco Serr\xc3\xa3o, the great friend of Magalh\xc3\xa3es, has\r\nperished some eight months previously from poison administered by the\r\nking of Tidore, whom he had visited, because he had aided the king of\r\nTernate against Tidore. This Serr\xc3\xa3o, says Pigafetta, was the cause of\r\nMagalh\xc3\xa3es undertaking his expedition, and he had been in the Moluccas\r\nfor ten years, for so long ago had Portugal discovered those islands.\r\nThe efforts of the Ternatans to gain the new strangers fail, for they\r\nare already pledged to the king of Tidore. On November 12, a house is\r\nbuilt ashore and on the thirteenth the merchandise is carried there,\r\namong it being that captured with the various junks at and near Borneo.\r\nThe sailors are somewhat careless of their bargains for they are in\r\nhaste to return to Spain. The king continues his kindness, and to humor\r\nhim, as he is a Mahometan, all the swine in the boats are killed. This\r\nrelation will be concluded in Vol. XXXIV.\r\n\r\n\r\n    The Editors\r\n\r\n    December, 1905.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nPRIMO VIAGGIO INTORNO AL MONDO\r\n\r\nBy Antonio Pigafetta. Signor che non \xc5\xbfolamente\r\n\xc5\xbfe contentano de \xc5\xbfapere et Intendere li grandi et admirabillj co\xc5\xbfe\r\nche dio me a conce\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfo de vedere et patire nela infra\xc5\xbfcripta mia\r\nlonga et pericolo\xc5\xbfa nauigati\xc3\xb5e. Jacobo de la \xc5\xbfpada piu volte c\xc5\x8d\r\nmolte \xc5\xbfue laude haueua peregrato in diuer\xc5\xbfe guize lo mare occeanno.\r\nMi parti c\xc5\x8d molte letere di fauore dela cita de bar\xc5\xbfalonna doue\r\nalhora re\xc5\xbfideua sua mage\xc5\xbfta et \xc5\xbfopa vna naue pa\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfay \xc5\xbfino amalega\r\nonde pigliando eL Camino \xea\x9d\x93 tera jun\xc5\xbfi a \xc5\xbfiuiglia et iui e\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfendo\r\n\xc5\xbftato ben circa tre me\xc5\xbfi e\xc5\xbfpetando que La dicta armata se pone\xc5\xbfe in\r\nhordine \xea\x9d\x93 la partita finalmente como qi de \xc5\xbfoto intendera v exa sa.\r\ncon felici\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfimi au\xc5\xbfpitij in comen\xc5\xbfiamo la nr\xcc\x83a nauigati\xc5\x8de Et\r\n\xea\x9d\x93ch\xcc\x83e ne le\xc5\xbfer mio in ytalia Quando andaua a la \xc5\xbfantita de papa\r\nClemente qella per \xc5\xbfua gratia amontero\xc5\xbfo ver\xc5\xbfo dime se dimo\xc5\xbftro\r\nassai benigna et humana et di\xc5\xbfsemi che li \xc5\xbfarebe grato li copia\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe\r\ntute qelle co\xc5\xbfe haueua vi\xc5\xbfte et pa\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfate nella nauigati\xc5\x8de Benche yo\r\nne habia hauuta pocha Como dita niente dimeno \xc5\xbfegondo el mio debiL\r\npotere li ho voluto \xc5\xbfati\xc5\xbffare. Et co\xc5\xbfi li oferi\xc5\xbfco in que\xc5\xbfto mio\r\nlibreto tute le vigilie fatiq\xca\x92 et peregrinati\xc5\x8de mie pregandola quando\r\nla vachera dalle a\xc5\xbfidue cure Rhodianne se degni tran\xc5\xbfcorerle peril\r\nque me potera e\xc5\xbfere n\xc3\xb5 pocho remunerato da. Volendo dar\r\nfine a que\xc5\xbfto que promi\xc5\xbfe c\xc3\xb5 Juramento aLo inperatore D. carlo Re de\r\n\xc5\xbfpagnia a\xc3\xa7io le naue nele fortune et nela nocte non se separe\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfeno\r\nvna de lalta. ordeno questo hordine et lo dete atuti li piloti et\r\nmae\xc5\xbftri de le \xc5\xbfue naui Loqual era lui de note \xc5\xbfempre voleua andar\r\ninanzi dele altre naui et elle \xc5\xbfeguita\xc5\xbfeno la \xc5\xbfua con vna facela\r\ngrande de legnio che la quiamano farol Qual \xc5\xbfemp\xcc\x83 portaua pend\xe1\xba\xbdte\r\nde la popa de la Sua naue que\xc5\xbfto \xc5\xbfegniale era acio de continuo lo\r\n\xc5\xbfeguita\xc5\xbfeno se faceua vno alto fuoco con vna lanterna ho c\xc3\xb5 vno pezo\r\nde corda de iuncho che la chiam\xc3\xa3 strengue di Sparto molto batuto neL\r\nhacqua et poi \xc5\xbfecado al \xc5\xbfole ho vero al fumo ottimo per simil cosa ge\r\nre\xc5\xbfponde\xc5\xbfeno a\xc3\xa7io \xc5\xbfape\xc5\xbfe per chesto \xc5\xbfegnialle che tute veniuano\r\nin\xc5\xbfieme se faceua duj focqi \xc5\xbfenza lo farolo vira\xc5\xbfseno o voltasenno\r\nin altra banda quando eL vento n\xc3\xb5 era buono et al prepo\xc5\xbfito \xea\x9d\x93 andar\r\nal nr\xcc\x83o camino ho q\xcc\x83do voleua far pocho viagio se faceua tre fuochi\r\ntole\xc5\xbfseno via la bonneta, che he vna parte de uela che se ataca da\r\nba\xc5\xbfso dela vela magiore quando fa bon tempo \xea\x9d\x93 andar piu la setol via\r\na\xc3\xa7io \xc5\xbfia piu facile aracogliere la vela magior quando se amayna in\r\npre\xc5\xbfsa in vno tempo subito: Si faceua quatro fochi amay\xc5\xbfseno tute le\r\nvele facendo poi lui vno \xc5\xbfegniale di fuoco como staua fermo Se faceua\r\npiu fochi ouero tiraua alguna b\xc3\xb5 barda fose segniale de tera o de\r\nbassi. \xc5\xbfe\xc5\xbfanta\r\ngiornj de continuo contra la opignione de li anticqi Jnanzi q\xcc\x83\r\najunge\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo ali legnea a 14 gradi molte gropade de venti inpetuo\xc5\xbfi\r\net corenti de acqua ne a\xc5\xbfaltaronno contra el viagio n\xc3\xb5 po\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfendo\r\n\xc5\xbfpontare Jnan\xc5\xbfi et acio q\xcc\x83 le naue n\xc3\xb5 pericula\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfeno. Se calauano\r\ntute le velle et de q\xca\x92\xc5\xbfta \xc5\xbforte andauamo de mare in trauer\xc5\xbfo fin\r\nq\xcc\x83 pa\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfaua la grupada \xea\x9d\x93che veniua molto furiosa. Quando pioueua\r\nn\xc3\xb5 era vento. Quando faceua \xc5\xbfolle era bonna\xc5\xbfa. veniuano aL bordo de\r\nle naue certi pe\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfi grandi q\xcc\x83 \xc5\xbfe quiamano tiburoni q\xcc\x83 anno denti\r\nteribilli et \xc5\xbfe trouano hominj neL mare li mangiano. pigliauamo molti\r\nc\xc3\xb5 hami de fero benche n\xc3\xb5 \xc5\xbfonno bonni da mangiare \xc5\xbfe non li picoli\r\net anche loro maL bonny. Jn que\xc5\xbfte fortune molte volte ne apar\xc5\xbfe il\r\ncorpo \xc5\xbfancto cioe \xc5\xbfancto elmo in lume fra le altre in vna\r\nob\xc5\xbfcuri\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfima nocte de taL \xc5\xbfplendore come e vna facella ardente in\r\ncima de La magiore gabia et \xc5\xbfte circa due hore et piu c\xc3\xb5 noi\r\ncon\xc5\xbfolandone q\xcc\x83 piangev\xc3\xa3o \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 quanto que\xc5\xbfta bennedeta luce\xc5\xbfe\r\nvol\xc5\xbfe partire da nuy tanto grandi\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfimo \xc5\xbfplendore dete ne li hocqi\r\nno\xc5\xbfti q\xcc\x83 \xc5\xbfte\xc5\xbfemo piu de mezo carto de hora tuti q\xcc\x83 n\xc3\xb5 haueua culo. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\r\nvn altra quando la femina vol far li oui li fa soura la \xc5\xbfquena deL\r\nma\xc5\xbfchio et iui \xc5\xbfe creanno n\xc3\xb5 anno piede et Sono di\xc5\xbfpo\xc5\xbfti homini et femine como noi \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\r\nMangiano carne humana de Li \xc5\xbfui nemici non \xea\x9d\x93 bonna ma \xea\x9d\x93 vna certa\r\nvzan\xc5\xbfa Que\xc5\xbfta vzan\xc5\xbfa Lo vno con laltro. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 fu principio vna vequia\r\nLaqalle haueua \xc5\xbfolamente vno figliolo q\xcc\x83 fu amazato dali suoi nemici\r\n\xea\x9d\x93 iL q\xcc\x83 pa\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfati alguni giorni li \xc5\xbfui pigliorono vno de la\r\nCompagnia q\xcc\x83 haueua morto Suo figliolo et Lo condusero doue \xc5\xbftaua\r\nque\xc5\xbfta vequia ela vedendo et ricordando\xc5\xbfe deL \xc5\xbfuo figliolo como\r\ncagnia rabiata li cor\xc5\xbfe ado\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfo et Lo mordete in vna \xc5\xbfpala co\xc5\xbftui\r\ndeli a pocho fugi neli \xc5\xbfoi et di\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe Como Lo vol\xc5\xbfero mangiare\r\nmo\xc5\xbftrandoli eL \xc5\xbfegnialle de La \xc5\xbfpala. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 q\xc3\xb1 que\xc5\xbfti pigliarono\r\npoi de qelli li mangiorono et qelli de que\xc5\xbfti \xc5\xbfiche \xea\x9d\x93 que\xc5\xbfto he\r\nvenuta tal vzan\xc5\xbfa. Se ve\xc5\xbfteno de\r\nve\xc5\xbftitur\xcc\x83 de piume de papagalo c\xc3\xb5 rode grande aL cullo de Le penne\r\nmagiore cosa ridicula ca\xc5\xbfi tuti li homini eccepto le femine et\r\nfanciuli hano tre bu\xc5\xbfi ne lauro de\xc5\xbfoto oue portano pietre rotonde et\r\nLongue vno dito et piu et meno de fora pendente. n\xc3\xb5 \xc5\xbfonno del tuto\r\nnegri ma oliua\xc5\xbftri \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 portano de\xc5\xbfcoperte le parte vergonio\xc5\xbfe iL\r\nSuo corpo e \xc5\xbfenza peli et co\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfi homini qaL donne Sempre Vano nudi iL\r\nSuo re e chiamato cacich \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 anno infiniti\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfimi papagali et ne danno\r\n8 ho 10 \xea\x9d\x93 vno \xc5\xbfpecho et gati maimoni picoli fati como leoni ma Jalli\r\nco\xc5\xbfa belissima \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 fano panne rotondo biancho de medola de arbore non\r\nmolto bonno q\xcc\x83 na\xc5\xbfce fra larbore et La \xc5\xbfcor\xc5\xbfa et he como recotta.\r\n\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 hanno porci q\xcc\x83 \xc5\xbfopa La \xc5\xbfquena teneno eL suo lombelico et vcceli\r\ngrandi q\xcc\x83 anno eL becho como vn cuquiaro \xc5\xbfen\xc5\xbfa linga \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 ne dauano\r\n\xea\x9d\x93 vno acceta ho cortello gr\xc3\xa3de vna ho due dele \xc5\xbfue figliole giouane\r\n\xea\x9d\x93 fchiaue ma \xc5\xbfua mogliere n\xc3\xb5 darianno \xea\x9d\x93 co\xc5\xbfa alguna \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Elle\r\nn\xc3\xb5 farebenno vergonia a suoi mariti \xea\x9d\x93 ogni gr\xc3\xa3 co\xc5\xbfa come ne \xc5\xbftate\r\nreferito \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 de giorno n\xc3\xb5 con\xc5\xbfenteno a li Loro mariti ma \xc5\xbfolam\xe1\xba\xbdte\r\nde nocte. Esse Lauorano et portano tuto eL m\xc3\xa3giar\xcc\x83 suo da li monti in\r\nzerli ho vero cane\xc5\xbftri \xc5\xbfuL capo ho atacati aL capo pero e\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfendo\r\n\xc5\xbfempre \xc5\xbfeco \xc5\xbfui mariti \xc5\xbfolam\xe1\xba\xbdte c\xc3\xb5 vno archo de verzin o de\r\npalma negra et vno mazo de freze di canna et que\xc5\xbfto fano per che\r\n\xc5\xbfonno gelo\xc5\xbfi \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 le femine portano \xc5\xbfui figlioli tacadi aL colo in\r\nvna rete de banbazo. Se\r\ndi\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe due volte me\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfa in tera \xea\x9d\x93 il que que\xc5\xbfti \xc5\xbftauano c\xc3\xb5 tanto\r\ncontricti\xc3\xb5e in genoquionj aL\xc5\xbfando le mano giunte q\xcc\x83 era grandisso\r\npiacere vederli \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Edificareno vna ca\xc5\xbfa per nui pen\xc5\xbfando\r\ndoue\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo \xc5\xbftar \xc5\xbfeco algun tempo et taglia rono molto ver\xc5\xbfin per\r\ndarnela a la no\xc5\xbftra partida \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 era \xc5\xbftato for\xc5\xbfe duy me\xc5\xbfi n\xc3\xb5\r\nhaueua pioue\xc5\xbfto in que\xc5\xbfta terra et Quando ajonge\xc5\xbfemo aL porto per\r\nca\xc5\xbfo piouete \xea\x9d\x93 que\xc5\xbfto deceuano noi vegnire daL cieLo et hauer\xcc\x83\r\nmonato no\xc5\xbfco la piogia \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 que\xc5\xbfti populi facilmente Se\r\nconuerterebenno a la fede de Je\xc5\xbfu xp\xc3\xb5.\r\n\r\nJmprima co\xc5\xbftoro pen\xc5\xbfauano li batelli fo\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfero figlioli de le naue et\r\nque elle li purturi\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfeno quando \xc5\xbfe butauano fora di naue in mare et\r\n\xc5\xbftando co\xc5\xbfi aL co\xc5\xbfta do como he vzan\xc5\xbfa credeuano le naue li\r\nnutri\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfeno \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Vna Jouene bella vene vn di nela naue capitania, houe\r\nyo \xc5\xbftaua non \xea\x9d\x93 alto \xc5\xbfenon \xea\x9d\x93 trouar\xcc\x83 alguno recapito \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 \xc5\xbftando\r\nco\xc5\xbfi et a\xc5\xbfpectando buto lo ochio supa la camera deL mai\xc5\xbfto et victe\r\nvno quiodo Longo piu de vn dito il que pigliando c\xc3\xb5 grande\r\ngentile\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfa et galantaria se lo fico aparte aparte de li labri della\r\n\xc5\xbfua natura et subito ba\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfa ba\xc5\xbfsa Se partite. Altre volte in que\xc5\xbfto fiume fu mangiado da questi Canibali per\r\ntropo fidar\xc5\xbfe vno Capitanio Spagniolo q\xcc\x83 \xc5\xbfe chiamaua Joh\xc3\xa3 de solis\r\net \xc5\xbfesanta homini q\xcc\x83 andauano a di\xc5\xbfcourire terra como nui.\r\n\r\nPo \xc5\xbfeguendo eL mede\xc5\xbfimo camino \xea\x9d\x9f\xc5\xbfo eL polo antarticho aco\xc5\xbfto de\r\nterra veni\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfimo adare in due J\xc5\xbfolle pienni de occati et loui marini\r\nveramente non \xc5\xbfe porla narare iL gr\xc3\xa3 numero de que\xc5\xbfti occati in vna\r\nhora carga\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfimo le cinque naue \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Que\xc5\xbfti occati \xc5\xbfenno negri et\r\nanno tute le penne aduno modo co\xc5\xbfsi neL corpo como nelle ale. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 n\xc3\xb5\r\nvolano et viueno de pe\xc5\xbfe \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 eranno tanti gra\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfi q\xcc\x83 non\r\nbi\xc5\xbfogniaua pelarli ma \xc5\xbfcor tiglarli anno lo beco como vno coruo\r\nQue\xc5\xbfti loui marini \xc5\xbfonno de diuer\xc5\xbfi colori et gro\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfi como viteli\r\net eL capo como loro c\xc3\xb5 le orechie picole et t\xc3\xb5de et denti grandi\r\n\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 n\xc3\xb5 anno gambe \xc5\xbfenon piedi tacade aL corpo \xc5\xbfimille a le nr\xcc\x83e\r\nmani c\xc3\xb5 onguie picolle et fra li diti anno qella pele. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 le ochie\r\n\xc5\xbfarebenno fe roci\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfime \xc5\xbfe pote\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfeno corere nodano et viueno de\r\npe\xc5\xbfcie \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Qui hebenno li naue grandi\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfima fortuna \xea\x9d\x93 il que ne\r\napar\xc5\xbfeno molte volte li tre corpi \xc5\xbfancti \xc3\xa7ioe sto. elmo sto. nicolo\r\net sta chiara et \xc5\xbfubito \xc5\xbfe\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfaua la fortuna.\r\n\r\nPartendone de qi ariua\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo fin a 49 gradi et mezo aL antarticho\r\ne\xc5\xbfsendo linuerno le naui introrono in vno bon porto \xea\x9d\x93 inuernar\xc5\xbfe\r\n\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 quiui \xc5\xbfte\xc5\xbfemo dui me\xc5\xbfi \xc5\xbfenza vedere \xea\x9d\x93\xc5\xbfonna alguna. Vndi a\r\nlinproui\xc5\xbfo vede\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo vno homo de \xc5\xbftatura de gigante q\xcc\x83 \xc5\xbftaua nudo\r\nnella riua deL porto balando cantando et butando\xc5\xbfe poluere Soura la\r\nte\xc5\xbfta. JL capitanio g\xc3\xb1ale mando vno deli nr\xcc\x83i a lui acio face\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe\r\nli mede\xc5\xbfimi acti in \xc5\xbfegno de pace et fati lo conduce in vna Jzolleta\r\ndinanzi aL capo g\xc3\xb1alle \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Quando fo nella \xc5\xbfua et nr\xcc\x83a pre\xc5\xbfentia\r\nmolto \xc5\xbfe marauiglio et faceua \xc5\xbfegni c\xc3\xb5 vno dito alzato credendo\r\nveni\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo daL ciello \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Que\xc5\xbfto erra tanto grande q\xcc\x83 li dauamo a\r\nLa cintura et ben di\xc5\xbfpo\xc5\xbfto haueua La faza grande et depinta intorno\r\nde ro\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfo et Jntorno li ochi de Jallo c\xc3\xb5 dui cori depinti in mezo de\r\nle galte. li pocqi capili q\xcc\x83 haueua erano tinti de biancho. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 era\r\nve\xc5\xbftito de pelle de animale co\xc5\xbfi de Sotilmente in\xc5\xbfieme \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 el\r\nqualle animalle a eL capo et orechie grande como vna mula iL colo et iL\r\ncorpo como vno camello, le gambe de ceruo et La coda de caualo et\r\nnitri\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe como lui \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 ge ne \xc5\xbfonno a\xc5\xbfaysimi in que\xc5\xbfta tera haueua\r\na li piedi albarghe de le mede\xc5\xbfme pelle q\xcc\x83 copreno li piedi a vzo de\r\n\xc5\xbfcarpe et nella mano vno archo curto et gro\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfo. La corda alquando\r\npiu gro\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfa di qelle deL lauto fata de le budelle deL medemo animale\r\nc\xc3\xb5 vno mazo de frece de canna non molto longue inpenade como le\r\nno\xc5\xbftre \xea\x9d\x93 fore p\xc3\xb5te de pietra de fuoca biancha et negra amodo de\r\nfreze turque\xc5\xbfque facendole c\xc3\xb5 vn alta pietra. Lo capo genneralle li\r\nfece dare da mangiare et bere et fra le altre co\xc5\xbfe q\xcc\x83 li mo\xc5\xbftrete li\r\nmo\xc5\xbftro vno \xc5\xbfpequio grande de azalle. quando eL vide \xc5\xbfua figura\r\ngrandamente \xc5\xbfe \xc5\xbfpauento et \xc5\xbfalto in drieto et buto tre o quato de li\r\nno\xc5\xbfti homini \xea\x9d\x93 terra \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 da poy li dete Suonagli vno \xc5\xbfpequio vno\r\npetine et certi pater no\xc5\xbfti et mando lo in tera c\xc3\xb5 4 homini armati\r\n\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Vno \xc5\xbfuo compagnio q\xcc\x83 may vol\xc5\xbfe venire a le naue quando eL vite\r\nvenire co\xc5\xbftui c\xc3\xb5 li no\xc5\xbfti cor\xc5\xbfe doue \xc5\xbftauano li alti \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Se\r\nmi\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfeno in fila tuti nudi \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 ariuando li no\xc5\xbfti a e\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfi\r\ncomen\xc5\xbforono abalare et cantare leuando vno dito aL ciello et\r\nmo\xc5\xbftrandoli poluere bianca de radice de erba po\xc5\xbfta in pigniate de\r\ntera q\xcc\x83 la mangia\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfeno \xea\x9d\x93che non haueuano altra co\xc5\xbfa \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 li\r\nno\xc5\xbfti li feceno \xc5\xbfegnio doue\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfeno vegnire a le naui et que li\r\najuterebenno portare le \xc5\xbfue robe \xea\x9d\x93 il que Que\xc5\xbfti homini subito\r\npigliorono Solamente li \xc5\xbfui archi et le \xc5\xbfue femine cargate como asine\r\nportorono il tuto. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 que\xc5\xbfte n\xc3\xb5 \xc5\xbfonno tanti grandi ma molto piu\r\ngro\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe quando le vede\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfimo grandam\xe1\xba\xbdte \xc5\xbfte\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo \xc5\xbftupefati \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\r\nanno le tete longue mozo brazo. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 \xc5\xbfonno depinte et ve\xc5\xbftite como\r\nloro mariti \xc5\xbfinon dinanzi a la natura anno vna pele\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfina q\xcc\x83 la\r\ncopre \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 menavano quato de q\xca\x92\xc5\xbfti animali picoli ligadi c\xc3\xb5 ligami\r\namodo de caueza. Que\xc5\xbfta gente quanto voleno pigliare de que\xc5\xbfti\r\nanimale ligano vno de que\xc5\xbfti picoli a vno \xc5\xbfpino \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 poi veneno li\r\ngrandi \xea\x9d\x93 Jocare c\xc3\xb5 li picoli et e\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfi \xc5\xbftando a\xc5\xbfcon\xc5\xbfi li amazano\r\nc\xc3\xb5 Le freze. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 li no\xc5\xbfti ne candu\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfero a le naui dizidoto tra\r\nhomini et femine et foreno repartiti de due parte deL porto a\xc3\xa7io\r\npiglia\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfeno de li dicti animalj.\r\n\r\nDeli a 6. Jorni fu vi\xc5\xbfto vno gigante depinto et ve\xc5\xbftito de la\r\nmedi\xc5\xbfima \xc5\xbforta de alguni q\xcc\x83 faceuano legnia \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 haueua in mano vno\r\narcho et freze aco\xc5\xbftando\xc5\xbfe a li no\xc5\xbfti pima \xc5\xbfe tocaua eL capo eL\r\nvolto et eL corpo et iL \xc5\xbfimile faceua ali no\xc5\xbfti et dapoy leuaua li\r\nmani aL ciello. Quando eL capo g\xc3\xb1ale Lo \xc5\xbfepe. Lo mando atore c\xc3\xb5\r\nLo\xc5\xbfquifo et menolo in qella Jzola che era neL porto doue haueuano\r\nfacta vna ca\xc5\xbfa \xea\x9d\x93 li fabri et \xea\x9d\x93 meter li alcune co\xc5\xbfe de le naue.\r\nco\xc5\xbftui era piu grande et meglio di\xc5\xbfpo\xc5\xbfti de li alti et tanto trata\r\nbile et gratio\xc5\xbfo. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 \xc5\xbfaltando balaua et quando balaua ogni volta\r\ncazaua li piedi Soto tera vno palmo. Stete molti giorni c\xc3\xb5 nui tanto\r\nqeL bati\xc5\xbfa\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo chiamandolo Johannj cos chiaro prenuntiaua Je\xc5\xbfu\r\npater no\xc5\xbfter aue maria et Jouani como nui \xc5\xbfe non c\xc3\xb5 voce\r\ngroci\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfima. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 poi eL capo g\xc3\xb1ale li dono vna camiza vna cami\xc5\xbfota\r\nde panno brague\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe di pano vn bonet vn \xc5\xbfpequio vno petine \xc5\xbfonagli\r\net altre co\xc5\xbfe et mandolo da li sui \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 ge li ando molto alegro et\r\nc\xc3\xb5tento eL giorno \xc5\xbfeguente co\xc5\xbftui porto vno de quelli animali grandi\r\naL capo g\xc3\xb1ale \xea\x9d\x93 il que li dete molte co\xc5\xbfe acio ne porta\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe de li\r\nalti ma piu noL vede\xc5\xbfemo pen\xc5\xbfa\xc5\xbfemo li Suoi lo haue\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfero amazato\r\n\xea\x9d\x93 hauer\xcc\x83 conuer\xc5\xbfato c\xc3\xb5 nuy.\r\n\r\nPa\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfati 15 giorni vede\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo quato de que\xc5\xbfti giganti \xc5\xbfenza le \xc5\xbfue\r\narme \xea\x9d\x93 che le aueuano a\xc5\xbfco\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe in certi \xc5\xbfpini poi li dui che\r\npiglia\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo ne li in\xc5\xbfegniaro ogni vno era depinto diferentiatamente\r\n\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 JL capo genneralle retenne duy li piu Joueni et piu di\xc5\xbfpo\xc5\xbfti c\xc3\xb5\r\ngrande a\xc5\xbftutia \xea\x9d\x93 condurli in \xc5\xbfpagnia Se alta mente haue\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe facto\r\nfacilmente hauerebenno morto alguni de nui. La stutia q\xcc\x83 vzo in\r\nretenerli fo que\xc5\xbfta \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 ge dete molti cortelli forfice \xc5\xbfpeqi\r\n\xc5\xbfonagli et chri\xc5\xbftalino hauendo que\xc5\xbfti dui li mani pienne de le detti\r\nco\xc5\xbfe iL capo g\xc3\xb1ale fece portare dui para de feri q\xcc\x83 \xc5\xbfe meteno a li\r\npiedi mo\xc5\xbftrando de donnarli et elli \xea\x9d\x93 e\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfere fero li piaceu\xc3\xa3o\r\nmolto ma non \xc5\xbfapeuano Como portarli et li rincre\xc5\xbfceua la\xc5\xbfsarli n\xc3\xb5\r\nhaueuano oue meter\xcc\x83 qelle merce; et be\xc5\xbfogniauali tenerli co le mani\r\nla pelle q\xcc\x83 haueu\xc3\xa3o intorno li alti duy voleuano ajutarli \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 ma iL\r\ncapo n\xc3\xb5 vol\xc5\xbfe vedendo q\xcc\x83 li rincre\xc5\xbfciua la\xc5\xbfsiare qelli feri li\r\nfece \xc5\xbfegnio li farebe ali piedi et queli portarebenno via e\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfi\r\nri\xc5\xbfpo\xc5\xbfero c\xc3\xb5 la te\xc5\xbfta de \xc5\xbfi \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Subito aduno mede\xc5\xbfimo tempo li\r\nfece metere a tucti dui et quando linquiau\xc3\xa3o c\xc3\xb5 lo fero q\xcc\x83 trauer\xc5\xbfa\r\ndubitauano ma \xc5\xbfigurandoli iL capo pur \xc5\xbfteteno fermi a vedendo\xc5\xbfe poi\r\nde lingano Sbufauano como tori quiamando fortemente setebos q\xcc\x83 li\r\najuta\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfe agli alti dui apena pote\xc5\xbfimo ligarli li mani li\r\nmanda\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo a terra c\xc3\xb5 noue homine a\xc3\xa7io guida\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfeno li no\xc5\xbfti doue\r\n\xc5\xbftaua La moglie de vno de qelli haueuano pre\xc5\xbfi perche fortem\xe1\xba\xbdte c\xc3\xb5\r\n\xc5\xbfegni la lamentaua a\xc3\xa7io ella intende\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo. \xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 Niuno \xc5\xbfenza li\xc5\xbfentia deL re le puo vedere et \xc5\xbfe alguno\r\nhe trouato o di giorno o de nocte apre\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfo la caza del re he amazato\r\n\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0 co\xc5\xbfe da mangiare q\xcc\x83 era\r\nvna marauiglia forni\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfemo li naui de hacqua buona Que\xc5\xbfta hacqua\r\nna\xc5\xbfcie calda ma\xc5\xbfe \xc5\xbfta \xea\x9d\x93 \xc5\xbfpacio duna hora fora de \xc5\xbfuo fonte\r\ndiuenta frigidi\xc5\xbf\xc5\xbfima que\xc5\xbfto e \xea\x9d\x93 q\xcc\x83 na\xc5\xbfce neL monte delli\r\ngarofoli aL contrario Como \xc5\xbfe diceua in
